403.gcc Flags

These are flags that appear in the benchmark sources, categorized as to whether they are portability candidates, mandatory, or forbidden.

Sections

Selecting one of the following will take you directly to that section:

  • Portability Flags
  • Other Flags
  • Mandatory Flags
  • Forbidden Flags

Portability Flags

  • -DCRAY
  • -DCRAY2
  • -DCRAY_STACK
  • -DCRAY_STACKSEG_END
  • -DGCC_VERSION
  • -DHOST_WORDS_BIG_ENDIAN
  • -DPOSIX
  • -DSPEC_CPU_AIX
  • -DSPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL
  • -DSPEC_CPU_HPUX
  • -DSPEC_CPU_IRIX
  • -DSPEC_CPU_MACOSX
  • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAVE_BOOL
  • -DSPEC_CPU_SOLARIS
  • -DSPEC_CPU_WIN32
  • -DSPEC_CPU_WIN64
  • -DSPEC_CPU_XLC
  • -D_SYSTYPE_SVR4
  • -D_WIN32
  • -DSPEC_CPU_NEED_ALLOCA_H
  • -DSPEC_CPU_NOINLINE
    • -DCRAY
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DCRAY(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • CRAY appears 2 times! Assists with CRAY alloca issues

    • -DCRAY2
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DCRAY2(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • CRAY2 appears 2 times! Assists with CRAY alloca issues

    • -DCRAY_STACK
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DCRAY_STACK(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • CRAY_STACK appears 1 times! Assists with CRAY alloca issues

    • -DCRAY_STACKSEG_END
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DCRAY_STACKSEG_END(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • CRAY_STACKSEG_END appears 2 times! Assists with CRAY alloca issues

    • -DGCC_VERSION
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DGCC_VERSION(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • Setting this macro to a value other than its default is forbidden.

    • -DHOST_WORDS_BIG_ENDIAN
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DHOST_WORDS_BIG_ENDIAN(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • This flag indicates that the benchmark is being built on a big-endian system. it seems not to be needed unless FP words are a different order from int words.

    • -DPOSIX
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DPOSIX(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • This macro indicates that the benchmark is being built on a POSIX-compliant system. Its default value may not be changed.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_AIX
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_AIX(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_AIX is used so that IBM submitters don't have to bother specifying SPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL. It sets HAVE__BOOL

    • -DSPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL allows the compiler to indicate that it has the bool type.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_HPUX
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_HPUX(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_HPUX is used so that HPUX submitters don't have to bother specifying SPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL. It sets HAVE__BOOL, and also includes alloca.h.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_IRIX
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_IRIX(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_IRIX is used so that SGI submitters can have alloca.h included

    • -DSPEC_CPU_MACOSX
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_MACOSX(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_MACOSX indicates that that OS has the malloc.h header file.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAVE_BOOL
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_NO_HAVE_BOOL(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_NO_HAVE_BOOL allows the compiler to indicate that it hasn't the bool type.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_SOLARIS
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_SOLARIS(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_SOLARIS is used so that SUN submitters don't have to bother specifying SPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL. It sets HAVE__BOOL, and also includes alloca.h.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_WIN32
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_WIN32(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_WIN32 sets up types for gcc's compile time arithmetic, reflects the lack of a unistd.g file, sets the size and existence of the __int64 type, and sets the default page size on Windows.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_WIN64
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_WIN64(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_WIN64 sets up types for gcc's compile time arithmetic, reflects the lack of a unistd.g file, sets the size and existence of the __int64 type, and sets the default page size on Windows. It also sets a type of __int64 instead of long for 2 variables.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_XLC
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_XLC(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_XLC is used so that IBM submitters don't have to bother specifying SPEC_CPU_HAVE_BOOL. It sets HAVE__BOOL

    • -D_SYSTYPE_SVR4
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]D_SYSTYPE_SVR4(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • This macro indicates that the benchmark is being built on a System Vr4-type system.

    • -D_WIN32
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]D_WIN32(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • This macro indicates that the benchmark is being built on a Windows system.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_NEED_ALLOCA_H
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_NEED_ALLOCA_H(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)
    • Use this flag to force alloca.h to be included.
    • -DSPEC_CPU_NOINLINE
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_NOINLINE(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)
    • Use this flag to force inline to be NULL. Use not expected.

Other Flags

  • -Dalloca
    • -Dalloca
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]Dalloca(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • This allows alloca to be set to the compiler's preferred alloca by SPEC rules.

Mandatory Flags

  • -I.
  • -DSPEC_CPU_WINDOWS
    • -I.
    • -I\.(?:\s+|$)

    • This flag is set for all builds in Spec/object.pm.

    • -DSPEC_CPU_WINDOWS
    • (?:^|(?<=\s))[-/]DSPEC_CPU_WINDOWS(?:=\S*)?(?=\s|$)

    • SPEC_CPU_WINDOWS allows that the Windows C Preprocessor is a STDC one, and sets ssize_t to int
